## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This is a chemical reaction kinetics problem where the rate of change of concentration A is modeled as a function of time t and current concentration A. The task is to discover the rate law governing the reaction, which could range from simple nth-order kinetics to more complex mechanisms involving time-dependent effects.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction with single species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed-order / Michaelis-Menten: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, saturation kinetics)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with reverse reaction or constant source)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Second-order with equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate expression from complex mechanism)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (reaction with time-varying external influence)
- Fractional order with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (diffusion-limited or heterogeneous kinetics)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first and second order pathways)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type rate law)
- Oscillatory forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodically driven reaction system)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA/dt depends only on powers of A with no time dependence, this indicates a standard autonomous rate law from mass-action kinetics
- If dA/dt shows explicit time dependence beyond what A(t) provides, this suggests external forcing, photolysis, or time-varying conditions (temperature ramps, flow reactors)
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(K+A)) indicate enzyme-like saturation mechanisms where substrate binding sites become limiting
- A product term A*(c-A) suggests autocatalytic or logistic growth behavior where both reactant and product concentrations matter
- Polynomial expressions in A (quadratic, cubic) often arise from multi-step reaction mechanisms after applying steady-state approximations to intermediates
- Negative constant terms combined with concentration-dependent terms suggest competing production and consumption processes (reversible reactions or constant feed)
- Half-integer or fractional powers of A (e.g., A**0.5) indicate chain reaction mechanisms or surface-catalyzed reactions with dissociative adsorption
- Exponential dependence on time (not concentration) may indicate a temperature-programmed reaction where Arrhenius rate constant changes with a time-dependent temperature profile
